world continues to urbanize and grow, the race to build the tallest buildings shows no signs of slowing down. With advancements in technology and construction techniques, skyscrapers are reaching new heights like never before. In this article, we will explore the current top 10 tallest buildings in the world as of 2025, along with the reasons behind their impressive heights.\\n1. Burj Khalifa, Dubai, UAE  828 meters\\nThe Burj Khalifa in Dubai holds the title of the tallest building in the world since its completion in 2010. Standing at a staggering 828 meters, this iconic structure is a symbol of Dubais rapid development and prosperity. The skyscraper features a mix of residential, commercial, and hotel space, making it a true marvel of modern engineering.\\n2. Shanghai Tower, Shanghai, China  632 meters\\nThe Shanghai Tower is the second tallest building in the world and the tallest in China. Completed in 2015, this twisting tower stands at 632 meters and is a shining example of sustainable architecture. Its unique design allows for natural ventilation and energy efficiency, setting a new standard for tall buildings around the world.\\n3. Abraj Al-Bait Clock Tower, Mecca, Saudi Arabia  601 meters\\nLocated in the holy city of Mecca, the Abraj Al-Bait Clock Tower is the third tallest building in the world. Completed in 2012, this megastructure serves as a luxury hotel, shopping mall, and prayer space for pilgrims visiting the Grand Mosque. Its iconic clock face is one of the largest in the world, making it a prominent landmark in Meccas skyline.\\n4. Ping An Finance Centre, Shenzhen, China  599 meters\\nThe Ping An Finance Centre in Shenzhen is the fourth tallest building in the world and the tallest in China. Completed in 2017, this sleek skyscraper houses office space, a hotel, and observation decks offering stunning views of the city. Its futuristic design and cutting-edge technology have earned it international acclaim as a symbol of Chinas rapid growth.\\n5. Lotte World Tower, Seoul, South Korea  555 meters\\nThe Lotte World Tower in Seoul is the fifth tallest building in the world and the tallest in South Korea. Completed in 2016, this mixed-use skyscraper features luxury apartments, a hotel, offices, and a shopping mall. Its glass facade and tapering design make it a striking addition to Seouls skyline, attracting tourists and locals alike.\\n6. One World Trade Center, New York City, USA  541 meters\\nOne World Trade Center is the sixth tallest building in the world and the tallest in the United States. Completed in 2014, this iconic tower stands at 541 meters and serves as a memorial to the victims of the September 11th attacks. Its symbolic design and resilient construction have made it a beacon of hope and resilience for New Yorkers and visitors alike.\\n7. Guangzhou CTF Finance Centre, Guangzhou, China  530 meters\\nThe Guangzhou CTF Finance Centre is the seventh tallest building in the world and the second tallest in Guangzhou. Completed in 2016, this mixed-use skyscraper features office space, a hotel, and luxury apartments. Its sleek design and cutting-edge amenities have made it a popular destination for business travelers and residents alike.\\n8. Tianjin CTF Finance Centre, Tianjin, China  530 meters\\nTied for the seventh spot is the Tianjin CTF Finance Centre, also standing at 530 meters. Completed in 2019, this impressive skyscraper is part of a larger development project in Tianjins central business district. Its striking design and modern amenities have made it a symbol of Tianjins rapid growth and urbanization.\\n9. CITIC Tower, Beijing, China  528 meters\\nThe CITIC Tower in Beijing is the ninth tallest building in the world and the tallest in the Chinese capital. Completed in 2018, this futuristic skyscraper features office space, a luxury hotel, and observation decks offering panoramic views of Beijing. Its innovative design and sustainable features have earned it praise from architects and urban planners around the world.\\n10. TAIPEI 101, Taipei, Taiwan  508 meters\\nRounding out the top 10 tallest buildings in the world is TAIPEI 101 in Taipei, Taiwan. Completed in 2004, this iconic tower held the title of the tallest building in the world until the completion of the Burj Khalifa in 2010. Its unique pagoda-inspired design and advanced engineering have made it a symbol of Taiwans economic success and technological prowess.\\nEmerging Trends in Skyscraper Construction\\n1. Sustainable Design: With growing concerns about climate change and resource depletion, sustainable design has become a top priority for skyscraper developers. Green building practices, energy-efficient systems, and renewable materials are being incorporated into new projects to minimize environmental impact and reduce operational costs.\\n2. Mixed-Use Developments: To maximize space and revenue, developers are increasingly turning to mixed-use developments that combine residential, commercial, and leisure facilities in a single skyscraper. This trend not only promotes a sense of community and connectivity but also reduces the need for car travel and promotes a more sustainable urban environment.\\n3. Smart Technology: The integration of smart technology into skyscrapers is revolutionizing the way buildings are managed and operated. From automated lighting and climate control systems to IoT sensors and AI-powered analytics, smart buildings are becoming more efficient, comfortable, and secure for occupants.\\n4. Vertical Gardens: As cities become more densely populated, the incorporation of vertical gardens and green spaces in skyscrapers has become a popular trend. Not only do these green features improve air quality and reduce heat island effects, but they also provide a much-needed respite from the concrete jungle for residents and visitors.\\n5. Skybridges and Observation Decks: Skybridges and observation decks are increasingly being included in tall buildings to offer panoramic views of the city and create unique experiences for visitors. These elevated spaces serve as tourist attractions, event venues, and social hubs, adding value to the overall building design.\\n6. Parametric Design: Parametric design tools and generative algorithms are enabling architects to create complex forms and shapes that were previously impossible to build. This trend has led to the rise of sculptural and futuristic skyscrapers that push the boundaries of traditional design and construction methods.\\n7. Adaptive Reuse: In an effort to preserve historic buildings and reduce waste, developers are increasingly turning to adaptive reuse projects that repurpose existing structures into modern skyscrapers. This trend not only honors the heritage of the original building but also adds a layer of cultural richness and uniqueness to the urban fabric.\\nIn conclusion, the top 10 tallest buildings in the world as of 2025 are a testament to human ingenuity, ambition, and creativity. From the iconic Burj Khalifa in Dubai to the sustainable Shanghai Tower in China, each skyscraper represents a unique blend of design, technology, and functionality. As cities continue to grow and evolve, we can expect to see even taller and more innovative buildings shaping the skylines of tomorrow. The emerging trends in skyscraper construction point towards a future where sustainability, technology, and community are at the forefront of urban development, creating a more livable and resilient built environment for generations to come.\\nAlso It is eighth tallest in the world by 2025.\\n\\nThe Guangzhou CTF Finance Center has 111 above ground and five below ground floor and a shopping mall, offices, apartments and a hotel.\\n\\nThe gross floor area of the skyscraper is 507,681.0 m2 (5,464,633 sq ft), of which slightly more than 20% is not part of the skyscraper, but the podium is attached to it.\\n\\n07. People can see the city from above an observatory. On 8 November 2013, architects in Chicago and New York City began a debate about the height of the One World Trade Center and the Willis Tower.\\n\\nThey were saying that there was a possibility that Willis Tower was taller than the One World Trade Center.\\n\\nOn 12 November, a committee agreed that the antenna at the top is part of the building, so the One World Trade Center is taller than Willis Tower.\\n\\n06. As of 2017, it had the worlds second highest lift at a top speed of 74 km (46 mi) per second at 20.5.\\n\\nPlanning models for the Lujiazui Financial District dating back to 1993 plan for a close-knit group of three supersert skyscrapers. The first of these, Jin Mao Tower, was completed in 1999; The adjacent Shanghai World Financial Center (SWFC) opened in 2008.\\n\\nShanghai Tower is the third tallest building in the world by 2025. It is the second tallest building in the world surpassing the Shanghai Tower at 632 meters, with the spire to be completed in November 2021. Merdeka 118 is the tallest in Malaysia and Southeast Asia.\\n\\nIt surpassed the 451.9 m Petronas Twin Towers as the tallest building in Malaysia and the 461.2 m Landmark 81 as the tallest building in Southeast Asia, retaining these titles in its own right. Burj Khalifa (Dubai, United Arab Emirates)\\n\\nThe Burj Khalifa in Dubai is the tallest building in the world. [...] As noted, the Burj Khalifa is currently the tallest building in the world. A handful of other skyscrapers have held the title previously, including the Chrysler Building, Empire State Building, Sears Tower, and Taipei 101. [...] 7. One World Trade Center (New York, United States of America)\\n\\nAt the southern tip of Manhattan, One World Trade Center in New York is the seventh tallest building in the world.\", \"score\": 0.939919, \"raw_content\": \"Skyscrapers that seem to rise endlessly above the cities at their feet fascinate more than just architecture enthusiasts. And nothing proves that more than the tallest buildings in the world. Their striking design plays a part, no doubt, but their seemingly physics-defying existence is what really draws a viewers eye up. While tall buildings can be found all over the planet, most of the tallest are located in Asia. In fact, half of the building in this list are in China alone. Read on to learn about these wonders of engineering, where theyre located, and some of the fascinating stories behind them.\\n\\n15. Central Park Tower (New York, United States of America)\\n\\nCentral Park Tower (left) among other skyscrapers in New York City.\\n\\nSituated on Manhattans Billionaires Row, Central Park Tower is a 1,550-foot skyscraper by American firm Adrian Smith + Gordon Gill Architecture. Its bottom few floors are occupied by a Nordstrom department store, but the rest of the 98 levels are dedicated to luxury condos, making it the tallest primarily-residential building in the world.\\n\\n14. Wuhan Greenland Center (Wuhan, China)\\n\\nWuhan Greenland Center is Central Chinas tallest building.\\n\\nAnother Adrian Smith + Gordon Gill Architecture masterpiece, Wuhan Greenland Center is a 1,562-foot tower that reduces wind resistance and vortex action with its tapered tripod shape, rounded corners, and domed top. It was originally designed to be nearly 500 feet taller, but airspace regulations thwarted the lofty plans.\\n\\n13. International Commerce Center (Hong Kong)\\n\\nThe International Commerce Center in Hong Kong.\\n\\nThe International Commerce Center, designed by Kohn Pedersen Fox (KPF), was also supposed to rise even taller than its 1,588 feet, but laws forbade it from exceeding the height of the surrounding mountains. Even so, the skyscraper is the tallest structure in Hong Kong and 13th tallest around the globe. It sits atop the Elements mall and overlooks Victoria Harbour.\\n\\n12. Shanghai World Financial Center (Shanghai, China)\\n\\nShanghai World Financial Center in Shanghai.\\n\\nAdjacent to the taller Shanghai Tower, the Shanghai World Financial Center rises 1,614 feet into the sky. Because of its unusual shape, it has earned a tongue-in-cheek nickname: the bottle opener. It was also designed by KPF.\\n\\n11. Taipei 101 (Taipei, Taiwan)\\n\\nTaipei 101, in Taiwan's capital, is the 11th tallest building in the world.\\n\\nRising 1,667 feet tall, Taipei 101 towers well above the other rooftops in its namesake city. Its facade, which was inspired by traditional Chinese architecture, is decidedly less contemporary than that of most other super-talls on this list. The skyscraper mainly houses offices, but also restaurants and a viewing platform. Every New Years Eve, fireworks are set off from the roof, attracting celebrating spectators from all over the world.\\n\\n10. CITIC Tower (Beijing, China)\\n\\nBeijings China Zun Tower, the 10th tallest building in the world, has a distinct profile.\\n\\nBeijings tallest building is CITIC Tower, a skyscraper full of offices that stands at 1,732 feet tall. Its also known as China Zun for its distinctive silhouette that echoes a zun, an ancient Chinese vessel for wine. The design was a collaboration between the architecture firms Farrells and KPF.\\n\\n9. Tianjin CTF Finance Centre (Tianjin, China)\\n\\nTianjin, a port in northern China, is home to the Tianjin CTF Finance Center, the ninth tallest building in the world.\\n\\nIts not just similar names that the Tianjin CTF Finance Center and the Guangzhou CTF Finance Center have in commonthey're the same height too. Both towers come in at 1,739 feet. The Tianjin tower is recognizable for its softly curving glass walls that reduce exposure to wind, sun, and moisture. Designed by Skidmore, Owings & Merrill, it includes offices, apartments, retail space, and hotel rooms.\\n\\n8. Guangzhou CTF Finance Centre (Guangzhou, China)\\n\\nThe Guangzhou CTF Finance Center in Guangzhou, in southern China, is the eighth tallest building in the world.\\n\\nThe Guangzhou CTF Finance Center, on the other hand, is boxier in silhouette and sits atop an eight-story podium. The building houses offices, hotel rooms, and retail space. Forth Bagley, the lead architect on the project, used white glazed tiles for the vertical mullions of the structure, a nod to a local craft tradition. This soaring building is another from KPF.\\n\\n7. One World Trade Center (New York, United States of America)\\n\\nAt the southern tip of Manhattan, One World Trade Center in New York is the seventh tallest building in the world.\\n\\nAt 1,775 feet, One World Trade Center in New York is the tallest building in both the city and the country. By comparison, the Empire State Buildingwhich was once the tallest building in the worldis only 1,453 feet high. The skyscraper was designed by David Childs of Skidmore, Owings & Merrill and constructed on the site where the original World Trade Center towers stood until September 11, 2001. One World Trade Center is not only a soaring skyscraper, it also serves as a powerful memorial and symbol of resilience.\\n\\n6. Lotte World Tower (Seoul, South Korea)\\n\\nThe Lotte World Tower, the sixth tallest building in the world, has become a landmark in Seoul.\\n\\nThe Lotte World Tower is the tallest building in South Korea and the sixth tallest building in the world, with 1,821 feet to its name. Also designed by KPF, it holds offices, apartments, stores, a hotel, a concert hall, and a viewing platform.\\n\\n5. Ping An International Finance Centre (Shenzhen, China)\\n\\nShenzhen, which sits just to the north of Hong Kong, is home to the Ping An Finance Center, the fifth tallest building in the world.\\n\\nA 1,965-foot skyscraper that rises above Shenzhens skyline, the Ping An Finance Center was built to anchor the citys business district. The 100-story building is centered around an atrium space and serves as the headquarters for the Ping An Insurance company. It was designed by KPF too.\\n\\n4. Makkah Royal Clock Tower (Mecca, Saudi Arabia)\\n\\nThe Makkah Royal Clock Tower, the fourth tallest building in the world, is part of a complex with seven hotels.\\n\\nMakkah Royal Clock Tower, also known as Abraj Al Bait, reaches an astounding height of 1,972 feetand the clock on top is the largest in the world. The massive timepiece features faces on all four sides, each with a diameter of 141 feet. Makkah is part of the Clock Tower complex, which includes seven hotels that cater to the millions of pilgrims who visit Mecca each year. The Great Mosque of Mecca, Islams holiest site, is located less than a quarter-mile from the development.\\n\\n3. Shanghai Tower (Shanghai, China)\\n\\nLocated in one of China's financial capitals, the Shanghai Tower (pictured on the right) is the third tallest building in the world.\\n\\nShanghai Tower, which was designed by American architecture firm Gensler, rises 2,073 feet into the air, making it the tallest building in China. Among the many features that make the tower impressive is its nine different indoor zones, each with its own atrium, garden, and cafes. Its twisting shape is both aesthetically-pleasing and practical, as it reduces wind resistance. Plus, its situated directly next to Shanghai Financial Center, the sixth tallest building in the country.\\n\\n2. Merdeka 118 (Kuala Lumpur, Malaysia)\\n\\nMalaysia's capital, Kuala Lumpur, is home to the second tallest building in the world, the recently completed Merdeka 118.\\n\\nFormerly known as PNB 118, Merdeka 118 is the second tallest building in the world and the newest addition to this group of record-breakers. It was completed in 2023, coming in at 2,228 feet. Its original name was short for Permodalan Nasional Berhad, a Malaysian investment management company that developed the project and occupies most of the building. But its current name means independence in Malay and was chosen in honor of nearby Stadium Merdeka, the site of the countrys declaration of independence in 1957.\\n\\n1. Burj Khalifa (Dubai, United Arab Emirates)\\n\\nThe Burj Khalifa in Dubai is the tallest building in the world.\\n\\nBurj Khalifa currently holds the title of the tallest building in the worldand the one with the most floors. The 2,717-foot, 163-floor skyscraper comprises apartments, offices, and hotel rooms, as well as the worlds highest restaurant and the worlds highest viewing platform. Designed by Adrian Smith, the buildings construction began in 2004 and finished in 2010. Its named after Sheikh Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan, the former president of the UAE.\\n\\nFrequently Asked Questions\\n\\nAs noted, the Burj Khalifa is currently the tallest building in the world. A handful of other skyscrapers have held the title previously, including the Chrysler Building, Empire State Building, Sears Tower, and Taipei 101.\\n\\nAdrian Smith is the American architect behind the tallest tower in the world, Burj Khalifa. He designed the Dubai skyscraper while he was a principal at Chicago-based architecture firm Skidmore, Owings & Merrill, but the project was completed after he left the company and launched his own firm with Gordon Gill, which is aptly named Adrian Smith + Gordon Gill Architecture. The two men also designed the under-construction Jeddah Tower, a Saudi Arabia skyscraper that is expected to exceed the height of Burj Khalifa and assume the title of tallest building in the world.\\n\\nJeddah Tower, also known as Burj Jeddah, is a neo-futuristic skyscraper that is currently under construction in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia. It is planned to be 3,281 feet tallwhich would make it the first ever one-kilometer building. But fans will have to wait another few years to see if Jeddah Tower reaches its goals, since it isnt slated for completion until 2028. Builders first broke ground in 2013but then paused work in 2018 for five years. It has been reported that 63 of the 157 floors were finished as of October 2024. When Jeddah Tower does open its doors, its expected to offer residential, commercial, and office spaces. There will also be an observation deck and a Four Seasons hotel.\\n\\nThe two tallest buildings in the US, One World Trade Center and Central Park Tower, appear on this listbut the country boasts lots of other skyscrapers that qualify as super-tall according to the guidelines of the Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat. Anything taller than 984 feet makes the cut. Chicagos Willis Tower, commonly referred to as Sears Tower, is 1,450 feet, while New Yorks 111 West 57th Street, also known as Steinway Tower, is 1,428 feet. The tallest building west of the Mississippi River is Los Angeless Wilshire Grand Center, which stands at 1,100 feet.\\n\\nMore Great Stories From AD\\n\\nNot a subscriber?
